        })\r\n          )\r\n        )\r\n      )\r\n    )\r\n  )\r\n};\r\n\r\n```\r\n\r\nI discovered that there was a plugin called `next-compose-plugins` to improve the readability, but still, I didn't like it.\r\n\r\n## Describe the solution you'd like\r\n\r\nFinally created a  simple function who load the plugins in order: \r\n\r\n```\r\nconst loadNextPlugins = (n, l = 0) =>\r\n  n.length - 1 === l ? n[l](nextConfig) : n[l](loadNextPlugins(n, l + 1));\r\n```\r\n\r\nUniminifed version:\r\n```\r\nconst loadNextPlugins = (plugins, index = 0) => {\r\n  if (plugins.length - 1 === index) {\r\n    return plugins[index](nextConfig);\r\n  } else {\r\n    return plugins[index](loadNextPlugins(plugins, index + 1));\r\n  }\r\n};\r\n```\r\n\r\nSo a next.config.js file will look like this instead\r\n```\r\nconst withSass = require(\"@zeit/next-sass\");\r\nconst withFonts = require(\"next-fonts\");\r\nconst withCss = require(\"@zeit/next-css\");\r\nconst withPurgeCss = require(\"next-purgecss\");\r\nconst TerserPlugin = require(\"terser-webpack-plugin\");\r\nconst withOffline = require(\"next-offline\");\r\nconst optimizedImages = require(\"next-optimized-images\");\r\nconst { whitelistClassPurgeCss } = require(\"components-translations\");\r\nconst OptimizeCSSAssetsPlugin = require(\"optimize-css-assets-webpack-plugin\");\r\n\r\nconst nextConfig = {\r\n  enableSvg: true,\r\n  webpack(config, options) {\r\n    config.optimization.minimize = true;\r\n    config.optimization.minimizer.push(new TerserPlugin());\r\n\r\n    config.optimization.minimizer.push(\r\n      new OptimizeCSSAssetsPlugin({\r\n        cssProcessorPluginOptions: {\r\n          preset: [\"default\", { discardComments: { removeAll: true } }]\r\n        }\r\n      })\r\n    );\r\n\r\n    return config;\r\n  }\r\n};\r\n\r\nconst loadNextPlugins = (n, l = 0) =>\r\n  n.length - 1 === l ? n[l](nextConfig) : n[l](loadNextPlugins(n, l + 1));\r\n\r\nconst plugins = [\r\n  withOffline,\r\n  optimizedImages,\r\n  withCss,\r\n  withPurgeCss,\r\n  withFonts,\r\n "author_association": "CONTRIBUTOR", "body": "## Is your feature request related to a problem? Please describe.\r\n\r\nCreate React App [allows configuring a backend proxy](https://create-react-app.dev/docs/proxying-api-requests-in-development/) in their development server, which is quite handy in certain scenarios. Any request that does not match an existing asset or an index HTML page gets forwarded to a backend server, if `HOST` is specified. For example:\r\n\r\n```bash\r\n/ # served by CRA\r\n/whatever/autogenerated/chunk.js # served by CRA\r\n/favicon.ico # served by the backend server if /public/favicon.ico does not exist\r\n/any/path/to/non-existing/local/resource.json # served by the backend server\r\n```\r\n\r\nEssentially, they are just using a standard [webpack-dev-server proxy feature](https://webpack.js.org/configuration/dev-server/#devserverproxy) as far as I understand.\r\n\r\nI\u2019ve been trying to configure our Next.js development server in a similar way but failed. We probably need to make a small tweak to the framework unless I\u2019m missing something. Here\u2019s roughly what I tried in the first place:\r\n\r\n```js\r\n// server.js\r\nconst next = require(\"next\")\r\nconst express = require(\"express\")\r\nconst proxyMiddleware = require(\"http-proxy-middleware\")\r\n\r\n;(async () => {\r\n  const app = next({ dev: true })\r\n  await app.prepare()\r\n\r\n  const expressServer = express()\r\n\r\n  // Handle requests using Next.js\r\n  const handle = app.getRequestHandler()\r\n  expressServer.all(\"*\", async (req, res) => {\r\n    await handle(req, res)\r\n  })\r\n\r\n  // Handle requests using the proxy middleware\r\n  expressServer.use(\r\n    proxyMiddleware(\"/\", {\r\n      target: `https://example.com`,\r\n      // a few more options\r\n    }),\r\n  )\r\n\r\n  expressServer.listen(3000, (err) => {\r\n    if (err) {\r\n      throw err\r\n    }\r\n    logger.log(\"Server ready on port 3000\")\r\n  })\r\n})()\r\n```\r\n\r\nIf I place Next.js handler before the proxy middleware handler, all requests are processed by Next.js. If I swap them, no requests reach Next.js anymore. This happens because both handlers are too greedy.\r\n\r\nI tried adding custom logic after `await handle(req, res)` to instruct express to ignore the just-obtained result from Next.js and proceed to the following hander. However, this did not work because response HTTP handers are already sent by then so cannot be rewritten. Even if it worked, it would be slow because for every request to proxy, Next.js would have to render a 404 page, which is then disposed.\r\n\r\n## Describe the solution you\u2019d like\r\n\r\nWe have a co-located restful API that can start with anything and unfortunately, the routing is outside our control. There is no shared prefix or pattern I can whitelist \u2013 otherwise, I could just place the proxy middleware handler first. API path examples:\r\n\r\n```\r\n/whoami\r\n/[USERNAME]/path/to/api/resource.json\r\n/[anything]/[you]/[can]/[imagine]\r\n```\r\n\r\nI\u2019d like to be able to proxy to all these paths in development just as I would do in CRA out of box. This means that I would like to somehow disable 404 page handling by Next.js.\r\n\r\nThis could look like:\r\n\r\n```js\r\n// Handle requests using Next.js\r\nconst handle = app.getRequestHandler({ skip404: true })\r\nexpressServer.all(\"*\", (req, res) => {\r\n  return handle(req, res)\r\n})\r\n\r\n// Handle requests using the proxy middleware\r\n// ...\r\n```\r\n\r\nI\u2019m not insisting on the option name or even its existence, this is just an example of what could potentially help. The same problem does not apply to production, because we export static app files and then serve them with Nginx. When testing the production build locally, we use a custom Express server and it works:\r\n\r\n```js\r\n// server.production.js\r\nconst express = require(\"express\")\r\nconst proxyMiddleware = require(\"http-proxy-middleware\")\r\n\r\nconst expressServer = express()\r\nexpressServer.use(\"/\", express.static(\"out\", { dotfiles: \"ignore\" }))\r\n// \u2191 not as greedy as Next.js handler, so Express proceeds to the below middleware\r\n// if a static file in 'out' dir is not found\r\n\r\nexpressServer.use(\r\n  proxyMiddleware(\"/\", {\r\n    target: `https://example.com`,\r\n    // a few more options\r\n  }),\r\n)\r\n\r\nexpressServer.listen(5000, (err) => {\r\n  if (err) {\r\n    throw err\r\n  }\r\n  logger.log(\"Server ready on port 5000\")\r\n})\r\n```\r\n\r\n## Describe alternatives you've considered\r\n\r\nFor now, I have to replace `\"*\"` with a regexp:\r\n\r\n```js\r\nconst handle = app.getRequestHandler({ skip404: true })\r\nexpressServer.all(/^\\/(_next\\/.*)?$/, (req, res) => {\r\n  return handle(req, res)\r\n})\r\n```\r\n\r\nThis works only for apps that:\r\n\r\n- have one entry point (just `pages/index.js`, no routing)\r\n- do not contain anything in the public directory\r\n\r\nThe solution is quite limiting and won\u2019t work for us in the long term.\r\n\r\n## Additional context\r\n\r\nI know there is an [RFC for plugins](https://github.com/zeit/next.js/issues/9133) and am wondering if this new abstraction could solve our problem. No matter if yes or no, I\u2019ve decided to share our team\u2019s issue to collect some feedback and ideas. Please describe.\r\n\r\nIt would be nice if we could pass custom `state` to `router.push`, same way it's done in browser (using `history.pushState`) so we could have same url, but different content.\r\nI would like to use this for a multistep/wizard form, which would be under some url (say `/form`) and keep the current step I'm on in history `state`. This way I could make it so the back button makes it go back a step.\r\nCurrently I couldn't find a solution to make this work, there's no way of providing this custom state & no way to intercept the browser \"back\" button.\r\n\r\n## Describe the solution you'd like\r\n\r\nExtra param for `router.push` allowing a object to be passed and saved to history `state`\r\n\r\n## Describe alternatives "CONTRIBUTOR", "body": "This would be useful, I had the same problem but I ended up solving it with hashes. When going a step forward transform the current step into a hash and use it with the `Router`, something like this:\r\n\r\n```js\r\nRouter.push({\r\n  pathname: '/wizard-form',\r\n  hash: convertIndexToHash(stepIndex),\r\n});\r\n```\r\n\r\nThen you end up with URLs like `/wizard-form`, `/wizard-form#two`, `/wizard-form#three`, and so on. I considered the absence of a hash as the first step. To listen to hashes changes, you can do this:\r\n```js\r\nconst handleHashChange = () => {\r\n  const stepIndex = convertHashToIndex(window.location.hash);\r\n  setCurrentStepIndex(stepIndex);\r\n};\r\n\r\nuseEffect(() => {\r\n  Router.events.on('hashChangeComplete', handleHashChange);\r\n  return () => {\r\n    Router.events.off('hashChangeComplete', handleHashChange);\r\n  }\r\n}, []);\r\n```"}}, "public": true, "created_at": "2019-10-23T15:40:37Z", "org": {"id": 14985020, "login": "zeit", "gravatar_id": "", "url": Loop Messages\n+ * ------------------------------\n+ * The bot will keep a message as the last one in a channel, with an interval between each post,\n+ * to keep important information more visible to users\n+ *\n+ * How it works:\n+ * At startup and repeatedly by a given interval, for each loop message, the bot will:\n+ * 1. Get the target channel of the loop message\n+ * 2. Fetch the last 50 messages of the channel\n+ * 3. If the last message is already the message we want to loop, do nothing (we don't want to spam the channel)\n+ * 4. Delete all loop messages (so the channel isn't filled with bot messages)\n+ * 5. Send the loop message\n+ */\n+\n+const loopMessages = require(\"./messages.js\");\n+\n+// time between each check to send a new loop message\n+const INTERVAL_TIME = 5 * 60 * 1000; // 5 minutes (ms)", ------------------------------\n+ * The bot will keep a message as the last one in a channel, with an interval between each post,\n+ * to keep important information more visible to users\n+ *\n+ * How it works:\n+ * At startup and repeatedly by a given interval, for each loop message, the bot will:\n+ * 1. Get the target channel of the loop message\n+ * 2. Fetch the last 50 messages of the channel\n+ * 3. If the last message is already the message we want to loop, do nothing (we don't want to spam the channel)\n+ * 4. Delete all loop messages (so the channel isn't filled with bot messages)\n+ * 5. Send the loop message\n+ */\n+\n+const loopMessages = require(\"./messages.js\");\n+\n+// time between each check to send a new loop message\n+const INTERVAL_TIME = 5 * 60 * 1000; // 5 minutes (ms)\n+\n+function getContent(loopMessage) {\n+  return loopMessage.trim();\n+}\n+\n+function isMessageFromBot(bot, message) {\n+  return message.author.id === bot.user.id;\n+}\n+\n+function isLoopMessage(messageToCheck, loopMessage, bot) {\n+  return (\n+    isMessageFromBot(bot, messageToCheck) &&\n+    messageToCheck.content.trim() === getContent(loopMessage.content)\n+  );\n+}\n+\n+async function sendLoopMessage(client, loopMessage) {\n+  const channel = client.channels.get(loopMessage.channelId);\n+  const channelMessages = await channel.fetchMessages({ limit: 50 303495936, "id": 336188507, "node_id": "MDI0OlB1bGxSZXF1ZXN0UmV2aWV3Q29tbWVudDMzNjE4ODUwNw==", "diff_hunk": "@@ -0,0 +1,75 @@\n+/**\n+ * ------------------------------\n+ * Loop Messages\n+ * ------------------------------\n+ * The bot will keep a message as the last one in a channel, with an interval between each post,\n+ * to keep important information more visible to users\n+ *\n+ * How it works:\n+ * At startup and repeatedly by a given interval, for each loop message, the bot will:\n+ * 1. Get the target channel of the loop message\n+ * 2. Fetch the last 50 messages of the channel\n+ * 3. If the last message is already the message we want to loop, do nothing (we don't want to spam the channel)\n+ * 4. Delete all loop messages (so the channel isn't filled with bot messages)\n+ * 5. Send the loop message\n+ */\n+\n+const loopMessages = require(\"./messages.js\");\n+\n+// time between each check to send a new loop message\n+const INTERVAL_TIME = 5 * 60 * 1000; // 5 minutes (ms)\n+\n+function getContent(loopMessage) {\n+  return loopMessage.trim();\n+}\n+\n+function isMessageFromBot(bot, message) {\n+  return message.author.id === bot.user.id;\n+}\n+\n+function isLoopMessage(messageToCheck, loopMessage, bot) {\n+  return (\n+    isMessageFromBot(bot, messageToCheck) &&\n+    messageToCheck.content.trim() === getContent(loopMessage.content)\n+  );\n+}\n+\n+async function sendLoopMessage(client, loopMessage) {\n+  const channel = client.channels.get(loopMessage.channelId);\n+  const channelMessages = await channel.fetchMessages({ limit: 50 });\n+\n+  // if the last message in the channel is from the bot, we don't need to send it again\n+  if (isLoopMessage(channelMessages.first(), loopMessage, client)) {\n+    return;\n+  }\n+\n+  // search through all the last messages for the loop message, so we can delete it\n+  channelMessages.forEach(message => {\n+    if (isLoopMessage(message, loopMessage, client)) {\n+      message.delete();\n+    }\n+  });\n+\n+  // now we can send the loop message in the channel\n+  channel.send(getContent(loopMessage.content));\n+}\n+\n+module.exports = {\n+  register: (client, logger) => {\n+    client.on(\"ready\", () => {\n+      const sendLoopMessages = () => {\n+        loopMessages.forEach(message => {\n+          sendLoopMessage(client, message);\n+        });\n+      };\n+\n+      setInterval(() => {\n+        sendLoopMessages();\n+      }, INTERVAL_TIME);\n+\n+      sendLoopMessages();", "path": "features/loopMessages/index.js", "position": 70,
